<div id="descriptionContainer">
      <div style="right:0" class="readable stacked" id="description">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer1059259424811394650">Silent Witness, is a story of rivalry, friendship, and loss, and how the tragedies of youth can change the course of our adulthood. It begins in 1967, in a small Midwestern town scarcely touched by the tumults of the decade. Seventeen-year-old Tony Lord, Lake City's star athlete, seems destined for great things. His driving ambition to move far beyond the narrow world of h</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText1059259424811394650">Silent Witness, is a story of rivalry, friendship, and loss, and how the tragedies of youth can change the course of our adulthood. It begins in 1967, in a small Midwestern town scarcely touched by the tumults of the decade. Seventeen-year-old Tony Lord, Lake City's star athlete, seems destined for great things. His driving ambition to move far beyond the narrow world of his parents and his hometown is precisely what attracts Alison Taylor, the beautiful and enigmatic daughter of the town's leading family, and it is what sets Tony apart from his two closest friends: Sam Robb — mercurial and charismatic, his only rival for athletic honors — and Sam's girl, Sue Cash, whose affection for Tony may mask something more.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="1059259424811394650">...more</a>

  <a href="/user/show/25063708-jen-warren" class="left imgcol" title="Jen Warren"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1410988006p2/25063708.jpg" alt="Jen Warren" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/958099470?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jun 04, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/25063708-jen-warren" class="user" title="Jen Warren">Jen Warren</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer958099470">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11767588841357619648">The blurb calls this psychological drama and suspense. I couldn't agree more. Though we're given two similar, unsolved crimes - decades apart - this story is as much about the relationship between Tony and Sam as it is finding out who was responsible for these murders.<br /><br />Though the narrative shifts from present to past, this author manages a clarity and cohesiveness that keep the pages turning. I was unable to guess the ending, and (rare for me), I didn't skim through the details to get there. Inst</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText11767588841357619648">The blurb calls this psychological drama and suspense. I couldn't agree more. Though we're given two similar, unsolved crimes - decades apart - this story is as much about the relationship between Tony and Sam as it is finding out who was responsible for these murders.<br /><br />Though the narrative shifts from present to past, this author manages a clarity and cohesiveness that keep the pages turning. I was unable to guess the ending, and (rare for me), I didn't skim through the details to get there. Instead, I enjoyed the suspense, the mystery, and the final, shocking conclusion.</span>

      <a href="/user/show/32648608-anne-martin" class="user" title="Anne Martin">Anne Martin</a>

              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1199666065">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13038864948696190602">I had read this book fifteen years ago, and found it while looking in the shelves of old books. I read it again and was amazed how much it had aged - or how much I did age...<br />First, in 67 or 68, there was no racism against catholic anymore. The nation had elected one yeas ago to be their president, and was willing to elect his brother now! Was the church you belong to that important then? maybe, it is difficult to look back and remember properly. What about racism? enough not to accept a black ma</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText13038864948696190602">I had read this book fifteen years ago, and found it while looking in the shelves of old books. I read it again and was amazed how much it had aged - or how much I did age...<br />First, in 67 or 68, there was no racism against catholic anymore. The nation had elected one yeas ago to be their president, and was willing to elect his brother now! Was the church you belong to that important then? maybe, it is difficult to look back and remember properly. What about racism? enough not to accept a black man in one of the junior clubs? I don't know.<br />Then, where girls willing to sleep with their high school boyfriends? before the pill? I don't think so. But once again, I may be wrong.<br />The story in itself is excellent and makes you wonder about life in a small American town. Of course, reading a book again is seldom as good as a first read for a suspense book. It is a fine one, for those of you who did not read it yet.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_890803104">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/890803104" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/5912519-bev-walkling" class="left imgcol" title="Bev Walkling"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1311947857p2/5912519.jpg" alt="Bev Walkling" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/890803104?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Mar 24, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/5912519-bev-walkling" class="user" title="Bev Walkling">Bev Walkling</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/590738.Silent_Witness" title=" 9780091792008" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/5912519-bev-walkling?shelf=legal" class="actionLinkLite">legal</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/5912519-bev-walkling?shelf=suspense" class="actionLinkLite">suspense</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/5912519-bev-walkling?shelf=relationship-issues" class="actionLinkLite">relationship-issues</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/5912519-bev-walkling?shelf=crime" class="actionLinkLite">crime</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/5912519-bev-walkling?shelf=fiction" class="actionLinkLite">fiction</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/5912519-bev-walkling?shelf=ethical-dilemma" class="actionLinkLite">ethical-dilemma</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer890803104">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5539273596025726948">Although this book is a book about a murder and the legal case that followed, even more it is the story of the relationship between Tony Lord and Sam Robb - friends from high-school. This is the second book that features Tony Lord and I have yet to read the first one though I plan to very shortly.<br /><br />Tony has been called back to his childhood town by an old friend when her husband is accused of the murder of a 16 year old student. He has an all too good understanding of what this is like because Ton</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText5539273596025726948">Although this book is a book about a murder and the legal case that followed, even more it is the story of the relationship between Tony Lord and Sam Robb - friends from high-school. This is the second book that features Tony Lord and I have yet to read the first one though I plan to very shortly.<br /><br />Tony has been called back to his childhood town by an old friend when her husband is accused of the murder of a 16 year old student. He has an all too good understanding of what this is like because Tony was himself accused (though never charged) with the murder of his high-school girl-friend.<br /><br />The first part of the book takes the reader back in time and explores the relationship between Tony, Sam and their girl-friends. Although Tony is never formally charged or found guilty, has has carried with him the suspicions of the people of his hometown and has never definitively learned who killed his girlfriend.<br /><br />The second part of the book returns to the present day and the lead up to the trial of Sam Robb. I won't go into detail for fear of spoiling things for the reader.<br /><br />I was pretty sure by chapter 12 that I knew who had murdered Tony's first girlfriend. Even knowing that, did not spoil my enjoyment of the story and the trial that followed. This was a tale well told! I highly recommend it to anyone who likes mysteries that fall into the legal genre.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="5539273596025726948">...more</a>

          </span>

          <a href="/book/show/107478.Silent_Witness" title="Hardcover 9780517361337" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1001925079">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer371363368549449899">Loved 'Silent Witness'. The characters, especially Tony Lord, were strong and clear. some of the subject matter was harsh related to the deaths of the two young girls, but I felt it value to the storyline. Seventeen year old Tony Lord left Lake City, OH for Harvard and never looked back. His girlfriend, Alison was brutally murdered as she sneaked out of her house late at night to meet him in the adjacent park. When she became an hour late, Tony went looking for her and found her bloodied body. H</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText371363368549449899">Loved 'Silent Witness'. The characters, especially Tony Lord, were strong and clear. some of the subject matter was harsh related to the deaths of the two young girls, but I felt it value to the storyline. Seventeen year old Tony Lord left Lake City, OH for Harvard and never looked back. His girlfriend, Alison was brutally murdered as she sneaked out of her house late at night to meet him in the adjacent park. When she became an hour late, Tony went looking for her and found her bloodied body. Her father arrived at the scene a few minutes after Tony and the teenager quickly became the prime suspect. His parents hired, Saul Ravin, the best criminal lawyer in the area and due to Saul's handling of things there was no indictment - not enough evidence - and eventually it was determined that a vagrant who hung around in the park was more the likely murderer. Tony was free in the end, but never truly exonerated. Tony's best friend, Sam Robb, tried to be supportive, but some of the things he did and didn't do or say left Tony feeling that Sam didn't believe him. Sam's girlfriend, Sue, was the only friend who stuck by Tony and before leaving town, Tony and Sue discovered they were in love. Sue said Sam needed her more, made the choice not to be with Tony and said goodbye. Fast forward 28 years, Tony is a high profile lawyer on the west coast, happily married to a famous actress and his phone rings. It's Sue, who is now married to Sam and she's asking him to come back to Lake City to help Sam, who is now vice-principal and coach at the high school. Sam is accused of murdering one of his students whom he was with on the night she died. Tony can't say 'no' to Sue - she seems so desperate; and, somehow, he is drawn back to the place he thought he had left behind with all its horrible memories. As soon as he arrives in Lake City, he is caught up in what 'was' and learns the horror of what 'is' as he expertly begins the process of trying to establish Sam's innocence. Tony is surprised at the depth of feelings that flood over him in Lake City, and he realizes how deeply he has pushed away the town's rejection of him. He visits Alison's grave, he tries to talk with her father, he reconnects with the aging - but still wise and savy - Saul, and his feelings for Sue come clear again. Sam is eventually indicted and a trial ensues. Saul agrees to work with Tony, his knowledge and experience are important, but his counsel, steadiness and objectivity are key for the younger lawyer. This is a long and detailed book, so I've only covered the barest surfaces of all that happened. The courtroom scenes and dynamics are amazing, the best I've ever read, and they kept the pace of the book strong. This is a clever mystery with a bang up ending, but the real story is about the relationship between these two men and Tony's relationship with Sue. We watch with hope as the events that unfold connect the dots of the past and the present for Tony. I highly recommend this book, whether you're a fan of mysteries or not.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="371363368549449899">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer7535844074331051502">First time reading this author. Picked this book up 10 years ago in Mexico...<br /><br />It was entertaining enough to hold my attention and get through it quickly. At 46, Tony Lord is a big time attorney in San Francisco, married to an Academy Award winner (second marriage). But he has his own terrible history from high school when his girlfriend Alison Taylor is murdered and he is the only suspect.<br /><br />His best friend, Sam Robb, and Sue Cash (now Sam's wife), call Tony with a plea for help. There has been anot</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText7535844074331051502">First time reading this author. Picked this book up 10 years ago in Mexico...<br /><br />It was entertaining enough to hold my attention and get through it quickly. At 46, Tony Lord is a big time attorney in San Francisco, married to an Academy Award winner (second marriage). But he has his own terrible history from high school when his girlfriend Alison Taylor is murdered and he is the only suspect.<br /><br />His best friend, Sam Robb, and Sue Cash (now Sam's wife), call Tony with a plea for help. There has been another murder and now Sam is the only suspect. Tony has to go to help, and will have to face his own demons.<br /><br />I liked the pace, and the intertwining of the past and present. The small town setting and characters were pleasant. In a lot of ways, I was reminded of Guilty as Sin by Tami Hoag that I read recently...but I liked this writing better. The back cover had a piece of the story that did not enter the story until almost half way in...it would have been better not knowing that. <br /><br />I did like the friendships and relationships developed, although something just didn't quite resonate fully with me on Sam and Tony's relationship...or Tony and Sue's for that matter. I couldn't put my finger on it, or what I would have changed. <br /><br />So...I liked this like I enjoy a legal thriller movie. There is another book that fills the gap of Tony's life from 18 to 45...if it were in my library I would definitely read it, but I'm not going out to buy it.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_134735832">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/134735832" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/4651948-jay-fromkin" class="left imgcol" title="Jay Fromkin"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1292179017p2/4651948.jpg" alt="Jay Fromkin" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/134735832?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Dec 12, 2010</a>

      <a href="/user/show/4651948-jay-fromkin" class="user" title="Jay Fromkin">Jay Fromkin</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/107478.Silent_Witness" title="Hardcover 9780517361337" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer134735832">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17408242056602506608">I haven't read a lot of legal thrillers - Scott Turow's first and a couple of John Grishams when trapped on an airplane. But Cousin Frank brought be a bag of paperbacks to help me get through post-surgical recovery. I'd never heard of Richard North Patterson (though my wife told me he was very popular). Having just started Patterson's "The Final Judgement), Patterson seems to have a standard set-up: an accomplished attorney has to return to his/her hometown, having previously vowed never to retu</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17408242056602506608">I haven't read a lot of legal thrillers - Scott Turow's first and a couple of John Grishams when trapped on an airplane. But Cousin Frank brought be a bag of paperbacks to help me get through post-surgical recovery. I'd never heard of Richard North Patterson (though my wife told me he was very popular). Having just started Patterson's "The Final Judgement), Patterson seems to have a standard set-up: an accomplished attorney has to return to his/her hometown, having previously vowed never to return. But he/she has a responsibility to prove a friend/relative innocent of murder. I didn't know that when reading "Silent Witness," so I just went along with the premise. In this case, it's super-attorney Tony Lord, who returns to his Ohio hometown to defend his high school best friend, Sam Robb - vice principal of his high school - against charges of murdering a student with whom he'd been having a sexual relationship. As a high school student, Tony had been accused of murdering his girlfriend, Alison Taylor, after having sex with her following the big football game which Tony, the quarterback, and Sam, the receiver won for their school. Tony is conflicted by his high school experience, his relationship with Sam, his relationship with Sam's wife, Sue, and his doubts about Sam's innocence. He is, however, a dedicated and determined criminal defense attorney, who will use any means at his disposal, including casting reasonable doubt by pointing a finger at another high school friend who knew the dead girl, Marcie Calder. <br /><br />While all of the lawyering keeps a level of suspense about Marcie's murder, it doesn't take Sherlock Holmes - or even Tony Lord - to figure out who murdered Marcie Calder and who murdered Alison Taylor. Patterson betrays the mystery through his characters' dialog - there's just too much yammering between and among the principal characters about Alison's murder, the night she died, the police investigation of Tony, the police investigation of Sam, how sorry everyone is about the murders and the accusations. Tony and Sam really are not very interesting characters, and Sue is just connective tissue. The most interesting characters are Stella Marz, a prosecutor with steel in her spine and a genuine outrage about crimes against women, and Saul Ravin, the aging attorney who had represented Tony in the matter of Allison Taylor and helped Tony in his defense of Sam Robb. <br /><br />What did I like? The high school friendship/competition between Tony and Sam was spot on in the details and genuine in its emotion. The two are both stellar athletes, but things just seem to come easier to Tony, which Sam resents. They are both candidates for the school's athlete of the year, which Sam wins but can't convince himself he was more deserving than Tony. He has a terrific girlfriend, but has convinced himself that Tony's is a better catch. When Tony comes back to defend Sam, he's conflicted between gratitude (though Sue asked Tony to defend Sam) and resentment against again falling into the shadow of the better athlete, who's now a legal legend. <br /><br />My wife was an attorney in another life, and I've sat on juries. As on TV and int he movies, Tony and Stella are the kind of lawyers we'd all like to have in a pinch - but which we rarely see in real life. The courtroom scenes are well done, with incisive questioning and anticipation of the opposition's questions; and dramatic, but not overly dramatic, opening and closing statements. Of course, we have the destruction of witness testimony and ingenious interpretations of evidence. The result of the trial is not surprising, but the denoument was. In the end the book really is about ethics - of police and prosecutors, educators, local politicians, victims' family members, and legal advocates.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="17408242056602506608">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_909808765">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/909808765" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/2685560-sandy-neal" class="left imgcol" title="Sandy Neal"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1252880488p2/2685560.jpg" alt="Sandy Neal" /></a>

<span id="freeTextContainer14429141418138479155">"Utterly compelling courtroom drama" is what it says on the back cover and I agree.<br /><br />Jumping back and forwards between high school and 28 years later present day this book tells the story of two close friends who are both joined in tragedies. The tragedies are murder, the circumstances have similarities, the rural town in Ohio hasn't changed but the two high school friends have followed different paths. <br /><br />I enjoyed reading the book.   <span style="display:none" id="freeText14429141418138479155">"Utterly compelling courtroom drama" is what it says on the back cover and I agree.<br /><br />Jumping back and forwards between high school and 28 years later present day this book tells the story of two close friends who are both joined in tragedies. The tragedies are murder, the circumstances have similarities, the rural town in Ohio hasn't changed but the two high school friends have followed different paths. <br /><br />I enjoyed reading the book. Yes, around half of it is set in a courtroom, but the character development and dialogue are well written and entertaining - you don't have to be a lawyer to enjoy the book. It was set in a legal context but it was really about the relationships between the main characters.<br /><br />Silent Witness makes me want to find some more Richard North Patterson books!</span>

  <span style="display:none" id="freeText11424656862181982190">Attorney Tony Lord left his hometown and the bitter memories of his girlfriend's murder behind. Now, twenty-eight years later, he's pulled back to Lake City to defend his closest high school friend against a charge of homicide. Sam Robb, the married father of two, is a local football legend. But he was also the last to see sixteen-year-old Marcie Calder alive, and as shocking forensic evidence at the trial reveals, he is the father of her unborn child. Probing the darkest recesses of love and friendship, Lord will discover things too disturbing to ignore--that Sam wasn't the only one in Lake City with a motive for killing Marcie, that small-town secrets can hide devastating betrayals, and that the past has a way of repeating itself . . . even in murder.</span>

  <span style="display:none" id="freeText3842332945782835826">28 years ago, Tony Lord was suspected but not formally tried for murdering his high school girlfriend. He was forced to handle the accusations of the town virtually alone. Once he graduated, he left the town, went to college, became a lawyer, and started a new life.<br /><br />That all changed when his former best friend was suspected of murder. He returns to his home town to help him, but he has no idea what he is walking into.<br /><br />This legal thriller by Patterson is a pretty easy read. Patterson explores the loyalty of friends and deals with the issue of sexual abuse of teenage girls by a trusted authority figure. I found the book to be a bit predictable, but entertaining.<br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer7717611654150566801">Like in most books of this type, the ending became obvious long before I got there, following the pattern of early "solutions" and red herrings, until it was obvious what was going to happen (unless something came out of left field - but that would spoil the fun, wouldn't it?) Still, it was well-written and I liked that it led me along by the hand rather than the nose. Good pacing (which is necessary in a book which which is long for this genre) and a reasonable plotline - although you did begin</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText7717611654150566801">Like in most books of this type, the ending became obvious long before I got there, following the pattern of early "solutions" and red herrings, until it was obvious what was going to happen (unless something came out of left field - but that would spoil the fun, wouldn't it?) Still, it was well-written and I liked that it led me along by the hand rather than the nose. Good pacing (which is necessary in a book which which is long for this genre) and a reasonable plotline - although you did begin to wonder if the police were so stupid as to not having pursued some obvious lines of inquiry, not to mention that the killer needed a LOT of luck to get away with the first killing.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_143924270">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/143924270" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/4852482-dick-edwards" class="left imgcol" title="Dick Edwards"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1295712575p2/4852482.jpg" alt="Dick Edwards" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/143924270?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 26, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/4852482-dick-edwards" class="user" title="Dick Edwards">Dick Edwards</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/107478.Silent_Witness" title="Hardcover 9780517361337" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer143924270">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1383402518733560160">This book held my interest until the end, when I was very disappointed. I did not think that the negative aspects of the character of the killer (whom I will not name here) were developed sufficiently to explain that person as a murderer. However, I hung in there until the end because it was an intriguing double mystery, the two halves separated by 28 years. The killer’s identity was not surprising enough, nor were there any major plot twists that I always like in a mystery. I give it a generous</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText1383402518733560160">This book held my interest until the end, when I was very disappointed. I did not think that the negative aspects of the character of the killer (whom I will not name here) were developed sufficiently to explain that person as a murderer. However, I hung in there until the end because it was an intriguing double mystery, the two halves separated by 28 years. The killer’s identity was not surprising enough, nor were there any major plot twists that I always like in a mystery. I give it a generous 5 (out of 10) because I approached the end with such anticipation.</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked &amp;&amp; exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;name=' + shelf_name + '&amp;a=' + action + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('aNnFNWdz05aG5huguxrsId44JOen2Wjg4ZwVLdU7PEMNDfrmlaHHbAo+bxvFewqTl8/n/u4EL0qLlRC/Ga7KBg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&amp;book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;refresh=true' + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('4mYx4ceevb9CJvNPrAoLGTzJ3o13QYlMJS1TGeULj4KHsg4yNUypRc7+h/TSa+2rdT4dlD6czuZPJFaLKZ55xw==')})
  }
//]]&gt;
</script>

    <div class=" clearFloats bigBox" id="aboutAuthor"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/38537.Richard_North_Patterson">About Richard North Patterson</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
      <a href="/author/show/38537.Richard_North_Patterson"><img alt="38537" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/authors/1219981953p2/38537.jpg" class="right" /></a>
    <div class="readable">
      
<span id="freeTextContainer1147415080749997139">Richard North Patterson is the author of fourteen previous bestselling and critically acclaimed novels. Formerly a trial lawyer, Patterson served as the SEC’s liaison to the Watergate special prosecutor and has served on the boards of several Washington advocacy groups dealing with gun violence, political reform, and women’s rights. He lives in San Francisco and on Martha’s Vineyard.<br /><a rel="nofollow" href="http://us.macmillan.com/author/richardnorthpatterson">Macmillan.com</a></span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText1147415080749997139">Richard North Patterson is the author of fourteen previous bestselling and critically acclaimed novels. Formerly a trial lawyer, Patterson served as the SEC’s liaison to the Watergate special prosecutor and has served on the boards of several Washington advocacy groups dealing with gun violence, political reform, and women’s rights. He lives in San Francisco and on Martha’s Vineyard.<br /><a rel="nofollow" href="http://us.macmillan.com/author/richardnorthpatterson">Macmillan.com Author Profile</a><br /><br />Awards<br />Edgar Award, 1980, Best First Novel for <a title="The Lasko Tangent, Degree of Guilt (Omnibus) by Richard North Patterson" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/107488.The_Lasko_Tangent__Degree_of_Guilt__Omnibus_">The Lasko Tangent</a><br /><br />Grand Prix de Littérature Policière, International Award, 1995 for <a title="Degree of Guilt by Richard North Patterson" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/481372.Degree_of_Guilt">Degree of Guilt</a><br /><br /><a rel="nofollow" href="http://us.macmillan.com/author/richardnorthpatterson" target="_blank">http://us.macmillan.com/author/richar...</a></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="1147415080749997139">...more</a>

    first = d.getElementsByTagName('SCRIPT')[0],
    n = load.length,
    i = 0,
    go = function () {
      for (i = 0; i &lt; n; i += 1) {
        script = d.createElement('SCRIPT');
        script.type = 'text/javascript';
        script.async = true;
        script.src = load[i];
        first.parentNode.insertBefore(script, first);
      }
    }
  if (w.attachEvent) {
    w.attachEvent('onload', go);
  } else {
    w.addEventListener('load', go, false);
  }
}(window, document,
